  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText5173743261733004515" style="display:none">From the author of the global phenomenon Ranger's Apprentice!<br /><br />They are outcasts. Hal, Stig, and the others - they are the boys the others want no part of. Skandians, as any reader of Ranger's Apprentice could tell you, are known for their size and strength. Not these boys. Yet that doesn't mean they don't have skills. And courage - which they will need every ounce of to do battle at sea against the other bands, the Wolves and the Sharks, in the ultimate race. The icy waters make for a treacherous playing field . . . especially when not everyone thinks of it as playing. John Flanagan, author of the international phenomenon Ranger's Apprentice, creates a new cast of characters to populate his world of Skandians and Araluens, a world millions of young readers around the world have come to know and admire. Full of seafaring adventures and epic battles, Book 1 of The Brotherband Chronicles is sure to thrill readers of Ranger's Apprentice while enticing a whole new generation just now discovering the books.<br /><br />Perfect for fans of J.R.R. Tolkien’s Lord of the Rings, T.H. White’s The Sword in the Stone, Christopher Paolini’s Eragon series, and George R. R. Martin’s Game of Thrones/A Song of Ice and Fire series.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_300892941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300892941" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300892941?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9781741664492" href="/book/show/13045888-the-outcasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=want">want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=australian">australian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300892941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2823774938437684496">As a fan of John Flanagan's Ranger's Apprentice series I was not sure what to expect with the first in his The Outcasts series. However I soon settled into this novel and came to appreciate and enjoy what he had written. Of course while his work is aimed predominantly at older children and younger teens it can be enjoyed by various age levels in my opinion. <br/><br/>There was a reasonable amount of various nautical terms floated around but nothing too technical. Flanagan does do an excellent job of helpi</span>
  <span id="freeText2823774938437684496" style="display:none">As a fan of John Flanagan's Ranger's Apprentice series I was not sure what to expect with the first in his The Outcasts series. However I soon settled into this novel and came to appreciate and enjoy what he had written. Of course while his work is aimed predominantly at older children and younger teens it can be enjoyed by various age levels in my opinion. <br /><br />There was a reasonable amount of various nautical terms floated around but nothing too technical. Flanagan does do an excellent job of helping the reader experience this almost historical world (after all his fantasy world is based on past civilisations) through the finer details without overloading them with information. But what really sells his work is the care he applies to his characters.<br /><br />Each character is no stereotype even though they may at times appear that way. And it would be easy for him to fall into using stereotypes. However he fleshes out each character as a unique and interesting creation in a very humble manner that's incredibly accessible to the reader. <br /><br />Flanagan's world is never kept too distant from the reader, his down to earth writing allowing reader's the chance to fall in love with what they read. Certainly some element of cliche exists in his work and he is no world-builder like Tolkien but what he does well is balance out the elements to create a story perfect for his target audience. He creates likeable characters, just enough details to realistically portray this as a real world and moreover adds warmth and passion to his writing. The characters and world come alive because the writer believes them to be and clearly loves writing for children and young teenagers.<br /><br />That all said I fully enjoyed this and look forward to seeing if he can develop this series into one equally as interesting as The Ranger's Apprentice. And do I encourage you to read this? Certainly and not only because John Flanagan is an Aussie with a nice down-to-earth manner of writing. I recommend this because I see that he writes books that subscribe to the perfect children's writer manual: they are accessible at ten and equally accessible at 15, 20, 30, 40 and so on. So read them simply to enjoy the storytelling ability and life of the books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2823774938437684496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_338119757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338119757" />
    <a title="Kit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6675293-kit"><img alt="Kit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318719334p2/6675293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338119757?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kit" href="/user/show/6675293-kit">Kit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338119757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18322916137699690267">HERE BE SPOILERS<br/><br/>Why, oh why, John Flanagan, must you create another wonderful book series and leave us on tenterhooks in a cliffhanger ending?<br/><br/>Ugh, I loved this book. It was very reminiscent of Ranger's Apprentice in the brotherly comradeship, and of course, some of the characters like Erak are recycled. Hal is very much like Will. Both are outcasts and have different talents than most people, but they find their place and turn out to have much talent. This is both good and bad, as I loved Will a</span>
  <span id="freeText18322916137699690267" style="display:none">HERE BE SPOILERS<br /><br />Why, oh why, John Flanagan, must you create another wonderful book series and leave us on tenterhooks in a cliffhanger ending?<br /><br />Ugh, I loved this book. It was very reminiscent of Ranger's Apprentice in the brotherly comradeship, and of course, some of the characters like Erak are recycled. Hal is very much like Will. Both are outcasts and have different talents than most people, but they find their place and turn out to have much talent. This is both good and bad, as I loved Will and Hal makes me feel like I'm reading about him again with all of his epic awesomeness, but this also had a downside in that it seems John Flanagan cannot write about other protagonists with character traits other than Will/Hal.<br /><br />Alright, so to the actual book. I really liked how the Skandian culture was shown through the boys being competing in brotherbands. They were being taught vital fighting skills and camaraderie at the same time, which to me really exemplifies the Skandian mindset of fighting and friendship, how when a person dies, they die with their sword in hand and all their friends around. <br /><br />Tursgud made me SO MAD. He was like a worse version of Horace. I loved the other boys though, especially Edvin, Hal, Stefan, and Jesper. I'd be happy to fight alongside or date any of them. <br /><br />Although, now that I think about it, that was one thing I didn't like. There was this random character Lotte, who seemed to just be put in for a distracting romantic interest for Hal. She was just there, and Hal didn't even think about her the same way that Will did Alyss. Perhaps she'll have a bigger role in later books, instead of a Mary Sue-esque pretty girl?<br /><br />I SO saw the whole conflict with Zavac coming; it was hard not to, but that's how John Flanagan intended it. Because the book was in omniscient pov, the reader sees Zavac's murder of the traders and how he intends to steal the Andomal (so brilliantly named 'thing'). But when the Herons were slated to guard the Andomal, I was like 'OH NO' because, obviously, Zavac was going to make a reappearance and try to steal it. I anticipated some serious stuff going down, but Hal was all like, "Imma go leave my incredibly important post to check if my boat's okay because a guy who was the FIRST MATE FOR THE OBERJARL OBVIOUSLY CAN'T TIE MAH BOAT WELL ENOUGH AND OBVIOUSLY NOTHING'S GONNA HAPPEN TO THE ANDOMAL BECAUSE IT'S BEEN SAFE FOR 300 YEARS HURR DURR DURR." I was literally screaming 'what the heck Hal how can you be so utterly moronic?' And then Zavac shows up and swipes the Andomal while the Herons are zonked out on the ground. Nice job guys. And then Erak throws his weight around and everyone's going to be a pariah so they decide to leave on a mission where they'll probably die. UGH CLIFFHANGERS. But seriously, John Flanagan did a great job of tying that together and making all suspenseful and whatever.<br /><br />Wow, this intelligent review has degenerated into me ranting psychotically. FIVE STARS; CAN'T WAIT FOR THE NEXT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18322916137699690267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_316881678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/316881678" />
    <a title="Nannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1218912-nannah"><img alt="Nannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507141437p2/1218912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/316881678?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nannah" href="/user/show/1218912-nannah">Nannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=series-i-won-t-finish">series-i-won-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=not-recommended">not-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer316881678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4235184801736316592">I'm sorry to say I didn't enjoy this book.<br/><br/>This is a young adult book, I understand, but I couldn't help but feel insulted by the writing. It was all function and nothing else, and worse than that it had so many repetitions and explanations of gestures that it made me think John Flanagan thought his readers would be idiots who didn't understand that when a character nodded it meant they agreed with something. Everything is told, nothing shown. I was TOLD that someone was angry or confused or happ</span>
  <span id="freeText4235184801736316592" style="display:none">I'm sorry to say I didn't enjoy this book.<br /><br />This is a young adult book, I understand, but I couldn't help but feel insulted by the writing. It was all function and nothing else, and worse than that it had so many repetitions and explanations of gestures that it made me think John Flanagan thought his readers would be idiots who didn't understand that when a character nodded it meant they agreed with something. Everything is told, nothing shown. I was TOLD that someone was angry or confused or happy, I was hardly ever shown it. And when it did occur, it happened with "in anger" or "in frustration" after it, so consistently redundant that I actually flinched every time it appeared, which was maybe fifteen plus times on a single page. The writing was awkward and contrived; I can't even count the number of times I saw the phrase, "as a result, . . . " <br /><br />The plot just a competition between boys. I was waiting for the plot to pick up into some romping adventure but it just sat there at a competition.<br /><br />The characters were flat, especially the boys in Hal's brotherband. One of them was a thief. Everything about him, every character trait had to do with the fact he was a thief. He run really fast, because he's a thief, I guess that would be a helpful trait if you were a thief (literally it was explained like that in the book). It's mentioned he's a thief almost every time his name comes up in paragraph. Or the "I'm short-sighted, not stupid" appeared in the dialogue at least two times. These characters had pretty much one defining feature and it was all they were throughout the entire novel. Not to mention the random love interest present in maybe two pages tops. I had forgotten about her until near the end she randomly kissed Hal. It's as if she was an afterthought, "oh yeah I need a girl character, she should probably just be a love interest but I don't want to deal with her so she'll appear just two times and it'll just be defending her from the antagonist and then a kiss for the hero."<br /><br />Exposition made up half the dialogue, all awkward and sounding out-of-character. I'm not actually sure what was in-character though, to be honest, everything was so stilted and cliche and written in one voice, all the characters could be the same if not for their defining feature. <br /><br />Sorry, I'm being really mean. It's my opinion only.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4235184801736316592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1155872701" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1155872701" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481754383p2/9740056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155872701?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101545393" href="/book/show/11534945-the-outcasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9740056-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155872701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7115817192957283880"><p>I really enjoyed the Ranger’s Apprentice series and when I noticed that Flanagan had written a spin off series based on the Skandians I thought that I might give it a read. I have been so disappointed in spin offs before that I wasn’t expecting much.</p><p>I just finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10551947.The_Outcasts__Brotherband_Chronicles___1_' title='The Outcasts (Brotherband Chronicles, #1) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Outcasts</a>, which is the first book of the Brotherband Chronicles, and I have to admit I was really pleased. The story revolves around a group of outcast teen boys and how they cope and compete in the Skandian society. If you’ve eve</p></span>
  <span id="freeText7115817192957283880" style="display:none"><p>I really enjoyed the Ranger’s Apprentice series and when I noticed that Flanagan had written a spin off series based on the Skandians I thought that I might give it a read. I have been so disappointed in spin offs before that I wasn’t expecting much.</p><p>I just finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10551947.The_Outcasts__Brotherband_Chronicles___1_" title="The Outcasts (Brotherband Chronicles, #1) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Outcasts</a>, which is the first book of the Brotherband Chronicles, and I have to admit I was really pleased. The story revolves around a group of outcast teen boys and how they cope and compete in the Skandian society. If you’ve ever been chosen last for a basketball game or teased because you weren’t as strong or as fast as the other kids, you’ll love this book. It’s full of great humor and edge of your seat excitement. The only problem I had with the book was how short the chapters were. I found myself saying, okay just one more chapter and then I’ll put it down. That won’t take long. Found myself reading way late into the night just to see what would happen next. </p><p>I’m very much looking forward to reading the second book of the series.</p><br /></span>

<div id="review_687751525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/687751525" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12279467-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364483953p2/12279467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687751525?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/12279467-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12279467-allison?shelf=youth">youth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12279467-allison?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12279467-allison?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12279467-allison?shelf=rebecca-caudill">rebecca-caudill</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer687751525&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687751525" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14467206854029836422">Part of my Caudill, Bluestem, Monarch challenge.<br/><br/>Thank goodness that's over. Usually I put books down within a few chapters of reading them if I don't like them. Unfortunately, I am reading this one for work and I had to slog my way through the entire thing screaming at Flanagan the whole way for his obnoxious writing style.<br/><br/>The main plot was actually decent if you can handle the fact that this was clearly a fictionalized group of people similar our Saxons. (Though it turns out our Saxons didn't a</span>
  <span id="freeText14467206854029836422" style="display:none">Part of my Caudill, Bluestem, Monarch challenge.<br /><br />Thank goodness that's over. Usually I put books down within a few chapters of reading them if I don't like them. Unfortunately, I am reading this one for work and I had to slog my way through the entire thing screaming at Flanagan the whole way for his obnoxious writing style.<br /><br />The main plot was actually decent if you can handle the fact that this was clearly a fictionalized group of people similar our Saxons. (Though it turns out our Saxons didn't actually have horned helmets as we like to envision them in...). With tighter writing, this would have been a phenomenal book. Sadly, instead of keeping this to one book or maybe two, Flanagan has decided to make it a series. And as a series, it's too much.<br /><br />Summary for potential BookTalks: Hal's father dies on a Skandian raid. He asks his best friend to look out for his son. Fast forward fifteen years (three chapters into the book of course...) and we see this kid is a bit of an outsider. He's built differently from most Skandians, mostly because his mother is Araluen. Thin and spry, Hal is very smart though not so good at physical feats of strength. So when it comes time for the Brotherband Training, he ends up with the rest of the people who don't fit into the tribe. Brotherband training, for those who don't know, is a passage of training for all the Skandian young men where they prove they are no longer boys but men. <br /><br />On top of this, there are also pirates! Everyone loves pirates EXCEPT FOR WHEN THEIR SOLE PURPOSE TO SET UP ANOTHER BOOK! Really Flanagan? They came out of nowhere it seemed! We're all looking to see what's happening with Hal and suddenly BAM pirates! <br /><br />The thing that bothered me the most though was how he had to tell us everything even to the point of repeating it to us. An example:<br /><br />One of the twins has been elbowing Ingvar in the ribs to keep him quiet. This is the following dialogue:<br /> " 'Cut it out! That hurts! Who is that, anyway?' He knew it was one of the twins, but he didn't know which one.<br /> Wulf saw the annoyed light in Invar's eyes and thought quickly. 'It's Ulf.'<br /> 'I'll settle with you later then,' Ingvar promised." <i>(Flanagan, p 169-70)</i><br /><br />At the end of the chapter, Hal notices that Ingvar keeps watching the twins.<br /> "Hal sighed in frustration. 'He's got something on his mind. I know it. I just wish I knew what it was.'<br /> That evening, they found out." <i>(Flanagan, pg 182).</i><br /><br />First of all, that's an awful transition into any chapter. That's the type of transition middle schoolers write in their papers when they're learning how to write. By adulthood, I would hope they know how to write more skillful transitions.<br /><br />The cream of this whole exchange comes when Ingvar finally looks for the twins.<br /> "Invar peered at him. blinking rapidly. 'One of you kept hitting me in the ribs this morning. Remember? And I said "Who's doing that" and whoever it was said, "It's Ulf.'<br /> Wulf suddenly grinned as understanding dawned. He'd elbowed Ingvar in the ribs when Gort was questioning him. And then he'd claimed to be his brother. Now, sensing that Ingvar was looking for retribution, he congratulated himself on his quick thinking." <i>(Flanagan, 184)</i><br /><br />Seriously? SERIOUSLY? He just summed it up for us twice on that page? How stupid does he think his readers are going to be unable to A) pick up on the fact that Ingvar was going to go after Ulf and B) forget what happened one chapter ago?<br /><br />And this is pretty much the entire book. We're told something is going to happen. We're told it's about to happen. And then we're reminded of what caused it to happen.<br /><br />Now I realize as an adult, I have better reading skills than most middle schoolers do. However, middle schoolers don't need this much hand holding. He breaks sentences with definitions of words because apparently people can't pick up on context clues. He tells the reader everything because apparently the reader is too dumb to understand that when someone nods, they clearly agree. <br /><br />Sadly, I will be recommending this book to 10 to 12 year old boys because they'll like the adventure aspect of it. I just wish I didn't have to because I hate seeing people read something so idiotically written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14467206854029836422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317318555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317318555" />
    <a title="Clare Cannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3655732-clare-cannon"><img alt="Clare Cannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416809580p2/3655732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317318555?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare Cannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare Cannon" href="/user/show/3655732-clare-cannon">Clare Cannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">9-14 years (boys)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655732-clare-cannon?shelf=08-12yrs">08-12yrs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3655732-clare-cannon?shelf=13-15yrs">13-15yrs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317318555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer617465455242771225"><a href='http://www.goodreadingguide.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Another brilliant adventure from the author of the Ranger's Apprentice series, for boys 9-14 (and anyone else who loves historical action-adventure... I thought it was great!). The scene setting in the initial chapters may be the only challenge for reluctant readers, but from chapter five the action begins when the boys are divided into brotherbands who must compete for the ultimate championship. Each challenge is bigger than the last, and among the unevenly matched teams we desperately hold</span>
  <span id="freeText617465455242771225" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.goodreadingguide.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Another brilliant adventure from the author of the Ranger's Apprentice series, for boys 9-14 (and anyone else who loves historical action-adventure... I thought it was great!). The scene setting in the initial chapters may be the only challenge for reluctant readers, but from chapter five the action begins when the boys are divided into brotherbands who must compete for the ultimate championship. Each challenge is bigger than the last, and among the unevenly matched teams we desperately hold out for the underdogs.<br><br>It's also a brilliant character story; amid the rivalry and action we see the best boys struggle against their weaknesses, learning what it means to work together toward a common goal. Leaders emerge, the good contrasted against the bad, and friendships are formed, challenged and formed again. Every character is unique, and it's plain their individual stories will likely develop further in the books to come.<br><br>In describing how the boys face each challenge Flanagan includes a good amount of tactical information, but rather than slowing the story it only makes you appreciate it more. Instead of just reading about it, we understand how they go about it: we feel Hal's skill in guiding his boat, we live the tactics of the tug-of-war, we experience the thrill (and the risk) of their plan for the night raid. We get so involved that we want to push the runners over the line by adding our voices to the shouts of the team. And because victories and defeats follow so closely on each other we can't rest for a moment.<br><br>The ending is a brilliant set up for another adventure and will have readers impatient for more. Lucky for me book 2 came out last week! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.GoodReadingGuide.com">www.GoodReadingGuide.com</a><br><br>**Forgot to mention that if you like this book you'll probably also like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3876030.A_Stranger_to_Command" title="A Stranger to Command by Sherwood Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">A Stranger to Command</a> which is for a slightly older readership, and one of my all time favourites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="617465455242771225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1646512413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1646512413" />
    <a title="Karis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38975931-karis"><img alt="Karis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546018277p2/38975931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1646512413?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karis" href="/user/show/38975931-karis">Karis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38975931-karis?shelf=friendships">friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38975931-karis?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38975931-karis?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646512413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17476932155036061029">I love this dear first book of the Brotherband Chronicles. It’s a coming of age book, but also a book written with an adult audience in mind as well, as many of the side and supporting characters are adults whose outlooks we get a glimpse into with Flanagan’s omniscient style of writing. <br/><br/><b>Owning your own personal responsibility despite current circumstances or challenges yet to come is the central theme of the book. </b>Creatively, John Flanagan teaches the lesson parallel in the lives of a young hal</span>
  <span id="freeText17476932155036061029" style="display:none">I love this dear first book of the Brotherband Chronicles. It’s a coming of age book, but also a book written with an adult audience in mind as well, as many of the side and supporting characters are adults whose outlooks we get a glimpse into with Flanagan’s omniscient style of writing. <br /><br /><b>Owning your own personal responsibility despite current circumstances or challenges yet to come is the central theme of the book. </b>Creatively, John Flanagan teaches the lesson parallel in the lives of a young half-Araluen Skandian boy named Hal and a former Skandian champion now feeling useless without his arm named Thorn. As Hal begins Brotherband training with the other Skandian boys, the training preparing them to become independent men, he’s suddenly thrust the role as skirl (captain) of his Brotherband—seven other boys, mostly misfits like him. He also learns more and more that Thorn’s advice is worth listening to and he’s not the old drunk that he is known as. <br /><br />I can’t help but think of this book as a mix of the <b>How to train your Dragon</b> movies (not the books), with Hal being a less dorky and quieter Hiccup but with the same tinkering and clever mindset, and the <b>Ranger’s Apprentice series</b> only with more sidekicks and on ships. So of course, I just had to love this book. My last read was my third through this story, and while I haven’t enjoyed the later books recently of the series, I will always love this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17476932155036061029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696183312" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11393286787449632793">Have I reviewed the Ranger’s Apprentice series? No?! Wait! What? Seriously! I can’t believe that I haven’t reviewed Ranger’s Apprentice. I really really need to review that series. It is like the best series ever! But, I am not reviewing that series right now. I am reviewing the first book in the Brotherband Chronicles, The Outcasts. <br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. It was super good and intriguing. Hal was a great main character, but do you know who I liked even more? Ladies and gentlemen, please we</span>
  <span id="freeText11393286787449632793" style="display:none">Have I reviewed the Ranger’s Apprentice series? No?! Wait! What? Seriously! I can’t believe that I haven’t reviewed Ranger’s Apprentice. I really really need to review that series. It is like the best series ever! But, I am not reviewing that series right now. I am reviewing the first book in the Brotherband Chronicles, The Outcasts. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It was super good and intriguing. Hal was a great main character, but do you know who I liked even more? Ladies and gentlemen, please welcome Thorn! Thorn was absolutely awesome! He was so cool! I felt bad for him at the beginning, especially because of the first chapter (or was it the prologue?). But, yes, I really liked Thorn. And, to be honest, I liked all of the Herons. Hal, Stig, Stefan, Ingvar, Edvin, Jesper were all awesome! I don’t know who I liked the best though, but for parts of the story I liked Stig the least. His temper tantrums were kind of annoying. I also liked the Wolves brotherband. They were pretty cool too.<br /><br />The cover was very cool. From what I saw online, there are a bunch of different covers, but I like the cover above the best. I would give it…3 stars.<br /><br />As for the book, I would definitely give it 4 stars. It isn’t Ranger’s Apprentice, but it was great! I would definitely recommend to all those who liked adventures! I can’t wait to read the rest of the series!<br /><br />Title: The Outcasts<br /><br />Author: John Flanagan<br /><br />Author’s Website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.worldofjohnflanagan.com/">http://www.worldofjohnflanagan.com/</a><br /><br />Reading Resolution: #25<br /><br />This review is written in my own opinions and words.</span>

<div id="review_252717043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252717043" />
    <a title="Tyrean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3212588-tyrean"><img alt="Tyrean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442623273p2/3212588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252717043?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tyrean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tyrean" href="/user/show/3212588-tyrean">Tyrean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252717043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer82815804053238474">Hal, an outcast mentored by an outcast, befriend by outcasts, is a well-written character in the midst of a somehwat expected plot. Yet, for all the familiarity of the plot, and even some of the characters, I thoroughly enjoyed this book. <br/><br/>Flanagan has a way of taking some familiar characters and giving them a new look and a new way of dealing with tough situations. <br/><br/>At first, it seems that Hal is up against his entire society, but we find that he has unexpected allies, and his wits serve him well</span>
  <span id="freeText82815804053238474" style="display:none">Hal, an outcast mentored by an outcast, befriend by outcasts, is a well-written character in the midst of a somehwat expected plot. Yet, for all the familiarity of the plot, and even some of the characters, I thoroughly enjoyed this book. <br /><br />Flanagan has a way of taking some familiar characters and giving them a new look and a new way of dealing with tough situations. <br /><br />At first, it seems that Hal is up against his entire society, but we find that he has unexpected allies, and his wits serve him well through expected and unexpected trials.The friendships that he builds, and the relationship with his mentor make this an unusually heart-warming book, and spur the adventure forward. <br /><br />If you enjoy fantasy action adventure with a little bit of alternative history (the Skandians are really Vikings in fantasy disguise), you'll enjoy The Outcasts, as well as John Flanagan's Ranger's Apprentice series. My family and I have read them all, and we are all looking forward to the next book in the Brotherband Chronicles.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer161462486985698783">This is the first book in the spin off series from the Rangers Apprentice series, and once again Flanagan does not disappoint. He writes fantastic characters with ethics and no need for gratuitous violence, swearing or sex making it perfect for middle grade readers.<br/>These remind me of "old school" stories where there is a more definitive line between good and evil ; and the good guys always win... or are at least rewarded somehow.<br/><br/>Great reading.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7088459017713630354" style="display:none">A very good tie-in to the world of Ranger's Apprentice &amp; strong start to the Brotherband series. <div id="review_2460574764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2460574764" />
    <a title="Anne-Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4736357-anne-marie"><img alt="Anne-Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528642325p2/4736357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2460574764?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne-Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne-Marie" href="/user/show/4736357-anne-marie">Anne-Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2460574764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2515234465318530053">Such a joy to read! <br/><br/>Hal is a great lead character. The creation of his brotherband is a compelling story about how they receive rigorous training to become cunning, skilled warriors, and compete with other local brotherbands. Hal grows convincingly into his natural role as an inspiring, fair but firm leader, and learns that leaders also make mistakes, that can have far reaching consequences. <br/>Hal’s relationship with Thorn, his dad’s best mate, is moving at times and a welcome addition to the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText2515234465318530053" style="display:none">Such a joy to read! <br /><br />Hal is a great lead character. The creation of his brotherband is a compelling story about how they receive rigorous training to become cunning, skilled warriors, and compete with other local brotherbands. Hal grows convincingly into his natural role as an inspiring, fair but firm leader, and learns that leaders also make mistakes, that can have far reaching consequences. <br />Hal’s relationship with Thorn, his dad’s best mate, is moving at times and a welcome addition to the story.<br /><br />The Skandian world resembles the Viking era, however, some of the language and attitudes seem very modern. I can’t imagine they spoke of things being 3-dimensional way back then, just to name an example. There were more things like this. <br /><br />This is the first book of a series so it ends on a cliffhanger, but it is still a satisfying, open ending if you’d prefer to not venture on to book 2. <br /><br />I will though!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2515234465318530053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_246199119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246199119" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246199119?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=homey">homey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=i-own-this">i-own-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246199119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4951132078274810859">First in the Brotherband Chronicles children's adventure-fantasy series revolving around eight young men of Hallasholm who are anxious to prove themselves to their peers and countrymen. This story is set several years after the events in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144350.The_Battle_for_Skandia' target='_blank' title='Opens John Flanagan's The Battle for Skandia in Goodreads' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>The Battle for Skandia</em>
</a>, 4, in the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br/><br/>In 2012, <em>The Outcasts</em> was nominated for the The Inky Awards for Gold Inky.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>The prologue is half-finished which made a reveal later in the story a bit confusing. I'm not really sure why Flanag</span>
  <span id="freeText4951132078274810859" style="display:none">First in the Brotherband Chronicles children's adventure-fantasy series revolving around eight young men of Hallasholm who are anxious to prove themselves to their peers and countrymen. This story is set several years after the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144350.The_Battle_for_Skandia" target="_blank" title="Opens John Flanagan's The Battle for Skandia in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Battle for Skandia</em>
</a>, 4, in the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br /><br />In 2012, <em>The Outcasts</em> was nominated for the The Inky Awards for Gold Inky.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />The prologue is half-finished which made a reveal later in the story a bit confusing. I'm not really sure why Flanagan bothered with a prologue.<br /><br />The main theme is team building as the eight primary characters — all outcasts in the village — come together as part of the brotherband training season. Secondary themes include strategy, humanity, and ingenuity.<br /><br />I liked the glossary explanations Flanagan provided; I had never thought to remember that "port" is "left" and they both have four letters. I've always remembered it as "pass the port on the left". Tells ya where my mind is at!<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />It's a critical year for Hal and Stig. They are 16 now and, with 26 others, will take part in the brotherband training this year. Teams are chosen much as kids today choose teammates, and there are a number of young men this year who know they will be chosen last or forced onto a team. And so it goes, Rollond and Tursgud have each chosen 9 other teammates and neither of them wants what's left; Erak makes his own choice and determines that the remaining eight will form the third brotherband.<br /><br />What follows is three months of training in tactics, weapon skills, seamanship, ship handling, and navigation and facing down Tursgud and the Sharks team. Proving themselves to each other, growing together as a team, and demonstrating their abilities to their people. Until that last day. The day when all falls apart.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Hal Mikkelson</strong> is Thorn's protégé and brilliant. He sees a way to make things better, and he does it from improvements to a crossbow to ideas on indoor plumbing to prosthetics to improved sail designs. Because his mother, <strong>Karin</strong>, was brought to Skandia as a slave, many in Hallasholm still see her as one even though Mikkel freed her as soon as he bought her. <strong>Stig</strong> is his best and only friend; his father stole from his shipmates and ran off years ago. Now his mother takes in laundry to survive. <strong>Wulf</strong> and <strong>Ulf</strong> are bickering twins; <strong>Edvin</strong> is good at math but so average in every way that most don't even notice him; <strong>Jesper</strong> has real talent as a thief and pickpocket; <strong>Stefan</strong> is the village clown and an expert mimic; and, <strong>Ingvar</strong> is very strong and very nearsighted. <br /><br /><strong>Tursgud</strong> leads one of the boys' cliques in Hallasholm; he's tall, well-built, athletic, handsome, and an arrogant bully always bragging about his father, the <strong>Maktig</strong>. <strong>Rollond</strong> is elected as the second team leader. <br /><br /><strong>Erak</strong> is Oberjarl of Skandia. <strong>Sigurd</strong> is responsible for the brotherband training while <strong>Gort</strong>, <strong>Jarst</strong>, and <strong>Viggo</strong> are in charge of a team each.<br /><br /><strong>Thorne</strong> was a mighty warrior until the voyage when he lost his hand saving the ship and his best friend, <strong>Mikkel</strong>, died; in the six years since he has degenerated into a staggering drunk until one night, <strong>Karin Mikkelswife</strong>, Mikkel's widow, saves him from himself.<br /><br /><strong>Zavac</strong> is the captain of a pirate ship plotting to steal Skandia's greatest treasure.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is chilling and exciting as I'm guessing that Hal is pulling on one of the sheets as the <em>Heron</em> and two other ships battle a storm at sea. It's a gorgeous figurehead on Hal's ship...the boys must have added that after this story ended because it sure ain't in this story. Nor is this particular scene. <br /><br />The title is very accurate for the eight boys are <em>The Outcasts</em> twice over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4951132078274810859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1287771778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1287771778" />
    <a title="Bregje (B a Reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7545577-bregje-b-a-reader"><img alt="Bregje (B a Reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540066889p2/7545577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287771778?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bregje (B a Reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bregje (B a Reader)" href="/user/show/7545577-bregje-b-a-reader">Bregje (B a Reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7545577-bregje-b-a-reader?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7545577-bregje-b-a-reader?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7545577-bregje-b-a-reader?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287771778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10351901379945458688">This review was also posted at <a href='http://booksarestories.blogspot.nl/2015/06/review-outcasts-by-john-flanagan.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Books are stories</a>.<br/><br/>The Ranger's Apprentice series is one of my favorite middle grade series. Although I loved that series I was a bit hesitant to start the Brotherband Chronicles, because this series would not have rangers as main characters and because of that I didn't think I would like this series as much. I did indeed enjoy the first Ranger's Apprentice book more than I enjoyed this first book, but it was a lot more fun than I expected it to be. Like the main ch</span>
  <span id="freeText10351901379945458688" style="display:none">This review was also posted at <a href="http://booksarestories.blogspot.nl/2015/06/review-outcasts-by-john-flanagan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Books are stories</a>.<br /><br />The Ranger's Apprentice series is one of my favorite middle grade series. Although I loved that series I was a bit hesitant to start the Brotherband Chronicles, because this series would not have rangers as main characters and because of that I didn't think I would like this series as much. I did indeed enjoy the first Ranger's Apprentice book more than I enjoyed this first book, but it was a lot more fun than I expected it to be. Like the main character of the other series the main character of this book, Hal, is a stubborn boy with a need to prove himself. Hal is an engineer and I thought that was a very interesting aspect of him. Throughout the book some of his inventions are mentioned, but I would have loved to read more about them.<br />Hal's crew is a diverse group of characters. I didn't get to know them too well, but there is a lot of potential for them to grow into more interesting characters. The twins Ulf and Wulf seemed more like caricatures and I hope they will get more complex personalities in later books.<br />Brotherband training was an interesting concept and I liked the different tasks the teams had to complete. It wasn't easy to predict how all the competitions would turn out and that kept the story interesting.<br />The story almost entirely plays around Hallasholm, the capital of Skandia, so I didn't really get to see any of the other places that I've come to love from the other series, but I get the feeling that in later books we will get to see those places again.<br />What I loved so much about the Ranger's Apprentice series was the humor. When the three characters Will, Halt and Horace were together this always resulted in hilarious banter. Flanagan tried to use Ulf and Wulf in this book as comic relief, but it just wasn't as strong as the banter in the other series. However, Hal definitely seems like a guy who can be very witty when he isn't so self concious, so hopefully he will grow over the span of the books and we will get some witty banter after all!<br />This book mostly seemed a set up for the rest of the series, but all in all I quite enjoyed it and I will definitely continue with the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10351901379945458688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tim Roast" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8073293-tim-roast"><img alt="Tim Roast" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594704873p2/8073293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289690392?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim Roast" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim Roast" href="/user/show/8073293-tim-roast">Tim Roast</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780370332277" href="/book/show/12993139-the-outcasts">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289690392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14942857396348555258">If you think Vikings on boot camp then that's pretty much what this book is.<br/><br/>The book begins with a guide to sailing terms with definitions to terms such as starboard and yardarm. Well, personally I would have put this at the end. Anyone picking this up and reading from the beginning might plough through this technical bit before giving up because it is a little bit of a chore, or was for me at least, and that would be a real shame.<br/><br/>After that false start the book follows 16-year-old Hal, a thinke</span>
  <span id="freeText14942857396348555258" style="display:none">If you think Vikings on boot camp then that's pretty much what this book is.<br /><br />The book begins with a guide to sailing terms with definitions to terms such as starboard and yardarm. Well, personally I would have put this at the end. Anyone picking this up and reading from the beginning might plough through this technical bit before giving up because it is a little bit of a chore, or was for me at least, and that would be a real shame.<br /><br />After that false start the book follows 16-year-old Hal, a thinker, who ends up in charge of a brotherband - brotherband teams being formed each year from the 16-year-olds in the town to compete against each other at a training camp with the purpose of training them for their futures as sea-faring warriors, such is the Skandian life. Unfortunately Hal ends up with the left-overs, the outcasts, the boys no-one else wanted in their team and he has reduced numbers too compared with the other two brotherbands. Nonetheless using Hal's ingenuity they perform well through the assessments.<br /><br />Simultaneously their town Hallasholm is being targeted by pirates which leads on nicely to the tale that will be covered by the next book in the series.<br /><br />The book has a bit of humour in it too which I enjoyed, especially during the night attack assessment.<br /><br />The hardcover version is beautiful with a nice shiny, well-designed cover and a spine with a number 1 at the top. It's obviously been designed for the bookshelf so that you can get the other books in the series, line them up and complete the collection. I notice the next couple of books are coming out as paperbacks though so you may want to get the paperback version of this one too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14942857396348555258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_252382238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252382238" />
    <a title="Brandon Slade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7272863-brandon-slade"><img alt="Brandon Slade" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252382238?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon Slade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon Slade" href="/user/show/7272863-brandon-slade">Brandon Slade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer252382238&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252382238" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14858285938405626140">This is the type of book that makes you happy as you're reading it. It is a tale of adventure, courage, and brotherhood. The outcasts in the Skandian society band together and form an inseparable group based on shared experiences and because of the fact that they're all outcasts. They make mistakes, but eventually realize the need for forgiveness. They don't get carried away with winning so much that they don't help out a fellow brotherband when they're in need. And they use all of their talents</span>
  <span id="freeText14858285938405626140" style="display:none">This is the type of book that makes you happy as you're reading it. It is a tale of adventure, courage, and brotherhood. The outcasts in the Skandian society band together and form an inseparable group based on shared experiences and because of the fact that they're all outcasts. They make mistakes, but eventually realize the need for forgiveness. They don't get carried away with winning so much that they don't help out a fellow brotherband when they're in need. And they use all of their talents to the best of their abilities, without letting pride or anger cloud their judgment.<br /><br />Then comes the whopper, at the end. (spoiler alert:) The Herons win the brotherband training, and they are rewarded with a night spend guarding the Skandian's most prized treasure. They biff it, due to various mistakes and accidents, and soon they are even more deserving of the title "outcast" than before. They lose a lot that they care about, but they know they deserve everything they got and more. It ends with a tragedy, but even in tragedy they hold together and decide to find, and take back, the treasure that they were supposed to guard. And this is where the second book comes in - the Invaders, coming May 2012.<br /><br />The author really did a great job mixing elements of victory and tragedy at the end. Even when it seems the outcasts will be hated for the rest of their lives for losing the Skandian's greatest treasure, they strike on the only possible solution: to right the wrong that they did by retrieving the treasure they lost.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14858285938405626140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10491666828539762881" style="display:none">I was hoping John Flanagan would never end The Ranger's Apprentice and was sad when he did, but then I saw this book was coming out and I immediately thought, "I have to read that." I am somewhat learned when it comes to sailing which made this book all the more enjoyable, with the sailor-term dictionary at the front of the book helping me along the way.<br />I love the way Hal is portrayed, he reminds me of Will. I think these new characters will definetly take some more getting used to, after all, it is only the first book of a hopefully long, adventurous series. I will miss the old characters but I will definetly enjoy re-reading those books, and at the same time meeting new characters and experiencing these new adventures and personalities for the first time.<br />I hate this whole cliff-hanger ending thing but I gotta admit, it sure guarentees I will read the next book. Not that I wouldn't read the sequel if he changed the ending(unless he totally botched it) because I can already tell I will like these new characters ever more so as the series progresses.</span>

I will go back and read the other Ranger's Apprentice at some point too, I'm sure. These are great adventure stories in a fun (so far) low magic fantasy world. Recommended.</span>

        <a title="Li&#39;l Izzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Li&#39;l Izzie" href="/user/show/55953432-li-l-izzie">Li&#39;l Izzie</a>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Li'l Izzie by: </span>
      my uncle
  </div>
